The most common types of host-guest interactions that affect electrochemical properties include:\n\n1. Electrostatic interactions: Binding of charged guests (such as metal cations or anions) to a host can alter the local charge environment, shifting redox potentials or affecting electron transfer rates.\n\n2. Hydrogen bonding: Formation or disruption of hydrogen bonds between host and guest can modulate the electronic environment of redox-active centers, leading to changes in current or potential.\n\n3. π-π stacking: Aromatic hosts interacting with aromatic guests can influence electron delocalization and redox behavior, often used in sensors for aromatic analytes.\n\n4. Coordination bonding: Hosts with metal centers can coordinate to guest molecules, changing the oxidation state or ligand field, which is directly reflected in electrochemical measurements.\n\n5. Inclusion/encapsulation: Encapsulation of a guest within a host cavity (e.g., cyclodextrins, cucurbiturils) can shield or expose redox-active sites, affecting their accessibility and electrochemical response.\n\n6.
